       <h1 itemprop="name" class="devsite-page-title"> Class Utilities </h1> 
       <nav class="devsite-page-nav-embedded devsite-nav"></nav>

         <div class="type doc"> 
          <span itemprop="name" style="display: none">Utilities</span> 
          <p>This service provides utilities for string encoding/decoding, date formatting, JSON manipulation, and other miscellaneous tasks.</p>

         <h2>Detailed documentation</h2> 
         <div id="base64Decode(String)" class="function doc "> 
          <h3 class="showalways"> <code itemprop="property">base64Decode(encoded)</code> </h3> 
          <p>Decodes a base-64 encoded string into a UTF-8 byte array. </p> 
          <pre class="prettyprint">
 
<code>
 // This is the base64 encoded form of "Google ????"
 var base64data = "R29vZ2xlIOOCsOODq+ODvOODlw==";

 // This will log:
 //     [71, 111, 111, 103, 108, 101, 32, -29, -126, -80,
 //      -29, -125, -85, -29, -125, -68, -29, -125, -105]
 var decoded = Utilities.base64Decode(base64data);
 Logger.log(decoded);

 // If we want a String instead of a byte array:
 // This will log the original "Google ????"
 Logger.log(Utilities.newBlob(decoded).getDataAsString());
 </code>
</pre> 
          <h4>Parameters</h4> 
          <table class="function param"> 
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <th>Name</th>
             <th>Type</th>
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td><code>encoded</code></td>
             <td><code>String</code></td>
             <td>an array of bytes of data to decode</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table> 
          <h4>Return</h4> 
          <p> <code>Byte[]</code>  the raw data represented by the base-64 encoded argument as a byte array</p> 
         </div> 
         <hr> 
         <div id="base64Decode(String,Charset)" class="function doc "> 
          <h3 class="showalways"> <code itemprop="property">base64Decode(encoded, charset)</code> </h3> 
          <p>Decodes a base-64 encoded string into a byte array in a specific character set. </p> 
          <pre class="prettyprint">
 
<code>
 // This is the base64 encoded form of "Google ????"
 var base64data = "R29vZ2xlIOOCsOODq+ODvOODlw==";

 var decoded = Utilities.base64Decode(base64data, Utilities.Charset.UTF_8);

 // This will log:
 //     [71, 111, 111, 103, 108, 101, 32, -29, -126, -80,
 //      -29, -125, -85, -29, -125, -68, -29, -125, -105]
 Logger.log(decoded);

 // If we want a String instead of a byte array:
 // This will log the original "Google ????"
 Logger.log(Utilities.newBlob(decoded).getDataAsString());
 </code>
</pre> 
          <h4>Parameters</h4> 
          <table class="function param"> 
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <th>Name</th>
             <th>Type</th>
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td><code>encoded</code></td>
             <td><code>String</code></td>
             <td>the string of data to decode</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td><code>charset</code></td>
             <td><code><a href="https://developers.google.com/apps-script/reference/utilities/charset.html">Charset</a></code></td>
             <td>a <code><a href="https://developers.google.com/apps-script/reference/utilities/charset.html">Charset</a></code> specifying the charset of the input</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table> 
          <h4>Return</h4> 
          <p> <code>Byte[]</code>  the raw data represented by the base-64 encoded argument as a byte array</p> 
         </div> 
         <hr>

         <div id="base64Encode(Byte)" class="function doc "> 
          <h3 class="showalways"> <code itemprop="property">base64Encode(data)</code> </h3> 
          <p>Generates a base-64 encoded string from the given byte array. Base 64 is a common encoding accepted by a variety of tools that cannot accept binary data. Base 64 is commonly used in internet protocols such as email, HTTP, or in XML documents. </p> 
          <pre class="prettyprint">
 
<code>
 // Instantiates a blob here for clarity
 var blob = Utilities.newBlob("A string here");

 // Writes 'QSBzdHJpbmcgaGVyZQ==' to the log.
 var encoded = Utilities.base64Encode(blob.getBytes());
 Logger.log(encoded);
 </code>
</pre> 
          <h4>Parameters</h4> 
          <table class="function param"> 
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <th>Name</th>
             <th>Type</th>
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td><code>data</code></td>
             <td><code>Byte[]</code></td>
             <td>a byte[] of data to encode</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table> 
          <h4>Return</h4> 
          <p> <code>String</code>  the base-64 encoded representation of the passed in data</p> 
         </div>

         <div id="base64Encode(String,Charset)" class="function doc "> 
          <h3 class="showalways"> <code itemprop="property">base64Encode(data, charset)</code> </h3> 
          <p>Generates a base-64 encoded string from the given string in a specific character set. A Charset is a way of encoding characters such that they can be encoded. These are typically done in a binary format, which can generally be incompatible with certain data transmission protocols. To make the data compatible, they are generally encoded into base 64, which is a common encoding accepted by a variety of tools that cannot accept binary data. Base 64 is commonly used in internet protocols such as email, HTTP, or in XML documents. </p> 
          <pre class="prettyprint">
 
<code>
 // "Google Groups" in Katakana (Japanese)
 var input = "Google ????";

 // Writes "R29vZ2xlIOOCsOODq+ODvOODlw==" to the log
 var encoded = Utilities.base64Encode(input, Utilities.Charset.UTF_8);
 Logger.log(encoded);

 </code>
</pre> 
          <h4>Parameters</h4> 
          <table class="function param"> 
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <th>Name</th>
             <th>Type</th>
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td><code>data</code></td>
             <td><code>String</code></td>
             <td>the string of data to encode</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td><code>charset</code></td>
             <td><code><a href="https://developers.google.com/apps-script/reference/utilities/charset.html">Charset</a></code></td>
             <td>a <code>Charset</code> specifying the charset of the input</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table> 
          <h4>Return</h4> 
          <p> <code>String</code>  the base-64 encoded representation of the input string with the given <code>Charset</code> </p> 
         </div>

         <div id="computeRsaSha256Signature(String,String,Charset)" class="function doc "> 
          <h3 class="showalways"> <code itemprop="property">computeRsaSha256Signature(value, key, charset)</code> </h3> 
          <p>Signs the provided value using RSA-SHA256 with the given key. </p> 
          <pre class="prettyprint">
 
<code>
 // This will write an array of bytes to the log.
 var signature = Utilities.computeRsaSha256Signature("this is my input",
     "-----BEGIN PRIVATE KEY-----\nprivatekeyhere\n-----END PRIVATE KEY-----\n");
 Logger.log(signature);
 </code>
</pre> 
          <h4>Parameters</h4> 
          <table class="function param"> 
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <th>Name</th>
             <th>Type</th>
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td><code>value</code></td>
             <td><code>String</code></td>
             <td>the input value to generate a hash for</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td><code>key</code></td>
             <td><code>String</code></td>
             <td>a PEM formatted key to use to generate the signature</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td><code>charset</code></td>
             <td><code><a href="https://developers.google.com/apps-script/reference/utilities/charset.html">Charset</a></code></td>
             <td>a <code><a href="https://developers.google.com/apps-script/reference/utilities/charset.html">Charset</a></code> representing the input character set</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table> 
          <h4>Return</h4> 
          <p> <code>Byte[]</code>  a byte[] representing the output signature</p> 
         </div> 
         <hr> 
         <div id="formatDate(Date,String,String)" class="function doc "> 
          <h3 class="showalways"> <code itemprop="property">formatDate(date, timeZone, format)</code> </h3> 
          <p>Formats date according to specification described in Java SE SimpleDateFormat class. Please visit the specification at <a href="http://docs.oracle.com/javase/7/docs/api/java/text/SimpleDateFormat.html"> http://docs.oracle.com/javase/7/docs/api/java/text/SimpleDateFormat.html</a> </p> 
          <pre class="prettyprint">
 
<code>
 // This formats the date as Greenwich Mean Time in the format
 // year-month-dateThour-minute-second.
 var formattedDate = Utilities.formatDate(new Date(), "GMT", "yyyy-MM-dd'T'HH:mm:ss'Z'");
 Logger.log(formattedDate);
 </code>
</pre> 
          <h4>Parameters</h4> 
          <table class="function param"> 
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <th>Name</th>
             <th>Type</th>
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td><code>date</code></td>
             <td><code>Date</code></td>
             <td>a <code>Date</code> to format as a String</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td><code>timeZone</code></td>
             <td><code>String</code></td>
             <td>the output timezone of the result</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td><code>format</code></td>
             <td><code>String</code></td>
             <td>a format per the <code>SimpleDateFormat</code> specification</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table> 
          <h4>Return</h4> 
          <p> <code>String</code>  the input date as a formatted string</p> 
         </div> 
         <hr> 
         <div id="formatString(String,Object...)" class="function doc "> 
          <h3 class="showalways"> <code itemprop="property">formatString(template, args)</code> </h3> 
          <p>Performs <code>sprintf</code>-like string formatting using '%'-style format strings. </p> 
          <pre class="prettyprint">
 
<code>
 // will be: " 123.456000"
 Utilities.formatString('%11.6f', 123.456);

 // will be: "   abc"
 Utilities.formatString('%6s', 'abc');
 </code>
</pre> 
          <h4>Parameters</h4> 
          <table class="function param"> 
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <th>Name</th>
             <th>Type</th>
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td><code>template</code></td>
             <td><code>String</code></td>
             <td>The format string that controls what gets returned.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td><code>args</code></td>
             <td><code>Object...</code></td>
             <td>Objects to use to fill in the '%' placeholders in the template.</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table> 
          <h4>Return</h4> 
          <p> <code>String</code>  the formatted string.</p> 
         </div> 
         <hr> 
         <div id="getUuid()" class="function doc "> 
          <h3 class="showalways"> <code itemprop="property">getUuid()</code> </h3> 
          <p>Get a UUID as a string (equivalent to using the <a href="https://docs.oracle.com/javase/7/docs/api/java/util/UUID.html"><code>java.util.UUID.randomUUID()</code></a> method). This identifier is not guaranteed to be unique across all time and space. As such, do not use in situations where guaranteed uniqueness is required. </p> 
          <pre class="prettyprint">
 
<code>
 //This assigns a UUID as a temporary ID for a data object you are creating in your script.
 var myDataObject = {
    tempId: Utilities.getUuid();
 };
 </code>
</pre> 
          <h4>Return</h4> 
          <p> <code>String</code>  a string representation of the UUID</p> 
         </div> 
         <hr> 
         <div id="newBlob(Byte)" class="function doc ">

         <div id="parseCsv(String)" class="function doc "> 
          <h3 class="showalways"> <code itemprop="property">parseCsv(csv)</code> </h3> 
          <p>Returns a tabular 2D array representation of a CSV string. </p> 
          <pre class="prettyprint">
 
<code>
 // This will create a 2 dimensional array of the format [[a, b, c], [d, e, f]]
 var csvString = "a,b,c\nd,e,f";
 var data = Utilities.parseCsv(csvString);
 </code>
</pre> 
          <h4>Parameters</h4> 
          <table class="function param"> 
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <th>Name</th>
             <th>Type</th>
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td><code>csv</code></td>
             <td><code>String</code></td>
             <td>a string containing a single or multiline data in comma-separated value (CSV) format</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table> 
          <h4>Return</h4> 
          <p> <code>String[][]</code>  a 2 dimensional array containing the values in the CSV string</p> 
         </div> 
         <hr> 
         <div id="parseCsv(String,Char)" class="function doc "> 
          <h3 class="showalways"> <code itemprop="property">parseCsv(csv, delimiter)</code> </h3> 
          <p>Returns a tabular 2D array representation of a CSV string using a custom delimiter. </p> 
          <pre class="prettyprint">
 
<code>
 // This will create a 2 dimensional array of the format [[a, b, c], [d, e, f]]
 var csvString = "a,b,c\td,e,f";
 var data = Utilities.parseCsv(csvString, '\t');
 </code>
</pre> 
          <h4>Parameters</h4> 
          <table class="function param"> 
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <th>Name</th>
             <th>Type</th>
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td><code>csv</code></td>
             <td><code>String</code></td>
             <td>a string containing a single or multiline data in comma-separated value (CSV) format</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td><code>delimiter</code></td>
             <td><code>Char</code></td>
             <td>between values</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table> 
          <h4>Return</h4> 
          <p> <code>String[][]</code>  a 2 dimensional array containing the values in the CSV string</p> 
         </div> 
         <hr> 
         <div id="sleep(Integer)" class="function doc "> 
          <h3 class="showalways"> <code itemprop="property">sleep(milliseconds)</code> </h3> 
          <p>Sleeps for specified number of milliseconds. Immediately puts the script to sleep for the specified number of milliseconds. The maximum allowed value is 300000 (or 5 minutes).</p> 
          <h4>Parameters</h4> 
          <table class="function param"> 
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <th>Name</th>
             <th>Type</th>
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td><code>milliseconds</code></td>
             <td><code>Integer</code></td>
             <td>The number of milliseconds to sleep.</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table> 
         </div> 
         <hr> 
         <div id="unzip(BlobSource)" class="function doc "> 
          <h3 class="showalways"> <code itemprop="property">unzip(blob)</code> </h3> 
          <p>Takes a Blob representing a zip file and returns its component files. </p> 
          <pre class="prettyprint">
 
<code>
 var googleFavIconUrl = "https://www.google.com/favicon.ico";
 var googleLogoUrl = "https://www.google.com/images/srpr/logo3w.png";

 // Fetch the Google favicon.ico file and get the Blob data
 var faviconBlob = UrlFetchApp.fetch(googleFavIconUrl).getBlob();
 var logoBlob = UrlFetchApp.fetch(googleLogoUrl).getBlob();

 // zip now references a blob containing an archive of both faviconBlob and logoBlob
 var zip = Utilities.zip([faviconBlob, logoBlob], "google_images.zip");

 // This will now unzip the blobs
 var files = Utilities.unzip(zip);
 </code>
</pre> 
          <h4>Parameters</h4> 
          <table class="function param"> 
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <th>Name</th>
             <th>Type</th>
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td><code>blob</code></td>
             <td><code><a href="https://developers.google.com/apps-script/reference/base/blob-source.html">BlobSource</a></code></td>
             <td>the zip file blob.</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table> 
          <h4>Return</h4> 
          <p> <code><a href="https://developers.google.com/apps-script/reference/base/blob.html">Blob[]</a></code>  a Blob[] representing the component blobs, each named with the full path inside the zip</p> 
         </div> 
         <hr> 
         <div id="zip(BlobSource)" class="function doc "> 
          <h3 class="showalways"> <code itemprop="property">zip(blobs)</code> </h3> 
          <p>Creates a new Blob object that is a zip file containing the data from the Blobs passed in. </p> 
          <pre class="prettyprint">
 
<code>
 var googleFavIconUrl = "https://www.google.com/favicon.ico";
 var googleLogoUrl = "https://www.google.com/images/srpr/logo3w.png";

 // Fetch the Google favicon.ico file and get the Blob data
 var faviconBlob = UrlFetchApp.fetch(googleFavIconUrl).getBlob();
 var logoBlob = UrlFetchApp.fetch(googleLogoUrl).getBlob();

 // zip now references a blob containing an archive of both faviconBlob and logoBlob
 var zip = Utilities.zip([faviconBlob, logoBlob]);
 </code>
</pre> 
          <h4>Parameters</h4> 
          <table class="function param"> 
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <th>Name</th>
             <th>Type</th>
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td><code>blobs</code></td>
             <td><code><a href="https://developers.google.com/apps-script/reference/base/blob-source.html">BlobSource[]</a></code></td>
             <td>a array of blobs to zip up</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table> 
          <h4>Return</h4> 
          <p> <code><a href="https://developers.google.com/apps-script/reference/base/blob.html">Blob</a></code>  a new blob containing the inputs as an archive</p> 
         </div> 
         <hr> 
         <div id="zip(BlobSource,String)" class="function doc "> 
          <h3 class="showalways"> <code itemprop="property">zip(blobs, name)</code> </h3> 
          <p>Creates a new Blob object that is a zip file containing the data from the Blobs passed in. This version of the method allows a filename to be specified. </p> 
          <pre class="prettyprint">
 
<code>
 var googleFavIconUrl = "https://www.google.com/favicon.ico";
 var googleLogoUrl = "https://www.google.com/images/srpr/logo3w.png";

 // Fetch the Google favicon.ico file and get the Blob data
 var faviconBlob = UrlFetchApp.fetch(googleFavIconUrl).getBlob();
 var logoBlob = UrlFetchApp.fetch(googleLogoUrl).getBlob();

 // zip now references a blob containing an archive of both faviconBlob and logoBlob
 var zip = Utilities.zip([faviconBlob, logoBlob], "google_images.zip");
 </code>
</pre> 
          <h4>Parameters</h4> 
          <table class="function param"> 
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <th>Name</th>
             <th>Type</th>
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td><code>blobs</code></td>
             <td><code><a href="https://developers.google.com/apps-script/reference/base/blob-source.html">BlobSource[]</a></code></td>
             <td>a array of blobs to zip up</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td><code>name</code></td>
             <td><code>String</code></td>
             <td>the name of the zip file to be created</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table> 
          <h4>Return</h4> 
          <p> <code><a href="https://developers.google.com/apps-script/reference/base/blob.html">Blob</a></code>  a new blob containing the inputs as an archive</p> 
         </div> 
         <h2>Deprecated methods</h2> 
         <div id="jsonParse(String)" class="function doc expandable"> 
          <h3 class="showalways"> <s><code itemprop="property">jsonParse(jsonString)</code></s> </h3> 
          <p class="warning deprecation"> <strong>Deprecated.</strong> As of November 2013, replaced by <code>JSON.parse()</code> </p> 
          <p>Return an object corresponding to the JSON string passed in. </p> 
          <pre class="prettyprint">
 
<code>
 // Returns the object { name: "John Smith", company: "Virginia Company"}
 var obj = Utilities.jsonParse('{"name":"John Smith","company":"Virginia Company"}');
 </code>
</pre> 
          <h4>Parameters</h4> 
          <table class="function param"> 
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <th>Name</th>
             <th>Type</th>
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td><code>jsonString</code></td>
             <td><code>String</code></td>
             <td>a String representation of a JavaScript object to deserialize</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table> 
          <h4>Return</h4> 
          <p> <code>Object</code>  a JavaScript object representation of the input</p> 
         </div> 
         <hr> 
         <div id="jsonStringify(Object)" class="function doc expandable"> 
          <h3 class="showalways"> <s><code itemprop="property">jsonStringify(obj)</code></s> </h3> 
          <p class="warning deprecation"> <strong>Deprecated.</strong> As of November 2013, replaced by <code>JSON.stringify()</code> </p> 
          <p>Return a JSON string of the object passed in. </p> 
          <pre class="prettyprint">
 
<code>
 // Logs: {"name":"John Smith","company":"Virginia Company"}
 var person = { name: "John Smith", company: "Virginia Company" };
 var json = Utilities.jsonStringify(person);
 Logger.log(json);
 </code>
</pre> 
          <h4>Parameters</h4> 
          <table class="function param"> 
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <th>Name</th>
             <th>Type</th>
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td><code>obj</code></td>
             <td><code>Object</code></td>
             <td>the JavaScript object to serialize to JSON</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table> 
          <h4>Return</h4> 
          <p> <code>String</code>  a JSON serialized JavaScript object</p> 
         </div>
